    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_31979042" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/31979042" />
    <a title="Ron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1256262-ron"><img alt="Ron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442983573p2/1256262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/31979042?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ron" href="/user/show/1256262-ron">Ron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Christians, seekers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256262-ron?shelf=christian_life">christian_life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256262-ron?shelf=religion-philosophy">religion-philosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256262-ron?shelf=lewis">lewis</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31979042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer367619119657538184">Re-reading <i>Four Loves</i> several years after my first reading I find a depth that I missed before. This last major work touching on Christianity by Lewis is less polemic and more analytic.<br/><br/>Going beyond the division of loves into gift-loves and need-loves, Lewis delves into how any affection can raise us bring us closer to divine source of love or move us farther away.<br/><br/>Not light reading, but worth it. More profound and challenging with each reading.<br/><br/>New review:<br/><br/>“Perhaps … all experience merely defines …</span>
  <span id="freeText367619119657538184" style="display:none">Re-reading <i>Four Loves</i> several years after my first reading I find a depth that I missed before. This last major work touching on Christianity by Lewis is less polemic and more analytic.<br /><br />Going beyond the division of loves into gift-loves and need-loves, Lewis delves into how any affection can raise us bring us closer to divine source of love or move us farther away.<br /><br />Not light reading, but worth it. More profound and challenging with each reading.<br /><br />New review:<br /><br />“Perhaps … all experience merely defines … the shape of that gap where our love of God ought to be.”<br /><br />As was often the case, C. S. Lewis’ take on love was thoughtful and out-of-step with the thinking of his day. Even more so our day. Five readings of this text have not demised the depth of thought and challenge found in these pages.<br /><br />This famous investigation of the four types of love exemplified by the Greek words <i>storge, philos, eros</i>, and <i>charios</i> begins with a preliminary discussion of gift-love versus need love. Lewis, like the scholar he was, defines terms and sets the stage for his greater argument.<br /><br />In the following 141 pages Lewis takes the reader on a relatively painless though deep investigation of just what love is and how we express it. Until the last chapter most of his examples arise from everyday life and his citations from literature and psychology. He assures that his reader is with him all the way.<br /><br />Finally as he expounds on charity Lewis of necessity moves into the supernatural. His references come more often from scripture. And that is because his definition of charity begins and ends with a gift-love of God. “Thou hast made us for thyself,” he quotes Augustine of Hippo “and our heart has no rest until it comes to Thee.” A love which not only transforms us but transforms how we love. “In my love for wife or friend the only eternal element is the transforming presence of Love Himself.”<br /><br />“All that was true love … was, even on earth, far more His than ours, and even ours only because His.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="367619119657538184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2733347596" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2733347596" />
    <a title="Tiff (fictionaltiff)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7621071-tiff-fictionaltiff"><img alt="Tiff (fictionaltiff)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577123213p2/7621071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2733347596?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiff (fictionaltiff)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiff (fictionaltiff)" href="/user/show/7621071-tiff-fictionaltiff">Tiff (fictionaltiff)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2733347596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11917830231767127289">Before reading The Four Loves, my perspective on love and its different meanings was but a hastily packed suitcase. A general understanding that Affection, Friendship, Romance (Eros), and Charity were all different ways to love and be loved was scattered in there, but not much beyond that. I was ready for the trip The Four Loves was going to take me on, but unaware of just how much I absolutely needed this book in my life.<br/>C.S. Lewis took my suitcase of thoughts, unpacked them, laid them before m</span>
  <span id="freeText11917830231767127289" style="display:none">Before reading The Four Loves, my perspective on love and its different meanings was but a hastily packed suitcase. A general understanding that Affection, Friendship, Romance (Eros), and Charity were all different ways to love and be loved was scattered in there, but not much beyond that. I was ready for the trip The Four Loves was going to take me on, but unaware of just how much I absolutely needed this book in my life.<br />C.S. Lewis took my suitcase of thoughts, unpacked them, laid them before me, then methodically organized everything into place, not leaving out a single detail; making sure everything had its right place before leaving me once again in complete awe of his genius and unique perspective on love.<br />The bits I was particularly fond of were his thoughts on Friendship as its own kind of love, set apart from Romance. From there Lewis dives into Divine love and explains just how different the love we receive from God can be from Romance. The romantic love people have for one another is enough to take someone on an entirely new course in life and it feels great, but the human heart is a fickle creature, whereas Charity love is constant and withstands all trials and hardship. But I’m no C. S. Lewis, so I’m going to stop there and let you all read it.<br />I can’t wait to discuss this one with my book club. It’s been added to my favorite C.S. Lewis list and was a perfect first book of the year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11917830231767127289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2506607308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2601550940768755312">Where most books on love give food for thought, THE FOUR LOVES offers a king's banquet. There is more wisdom in one page of this book than in the entirety of Erich Fromm's THE ART OF LOVING.<br/>Love is a messy subject, so it's only natural that Lewis' analysis be a bit messy as well. And though he's incredibly methodical in shaping his ideas and presenting them with art and diplomacy, Lewis writes with such warmth and accessibility that we view him as the sagely uncle we all dearly wish we had.<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('n0HJHD6m/YD5gITqy/2jnDooz/6YI+V+AOozicWmJ2ecxTz2VfRVe9axDAGs9E0s2V2NFplseaeHmFWRgWxgUw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Q5j4Jo7sJe/8Y+gJBc86250H0Hl/3BTLkd84wiUyFtxAHA3M5b6NFNNSYOJixtRrfnKSkX6TiBIWrV7aYfhR6A==')})
  }
//]]>

What did Jesus mean to say to us? What is his will for us today? Drawing on the Sermon on the Mount, Dietrich Bonhoeffer answers these timeless questions by providing a seminal reading of the dichotomy between &quot;cheap grace&quot; and &quot;costly grace.&quot; &quot;Cheap grace,&quot; Bonhoeffer wrote, &quot;is the grace we bestow on ourselves...grace without discipleship....Costly grace is the gospel which must be sought again and again, the girl which Chesterton, the &quot;Prince of Paradox,&quot; is at his witty best in this collection of twenty essays and articles from the turn of the twentieth century. Focusing on &quot;heretics&quot; — those who pride themselves on their superiority to Christian views — Chesterton appraises prominent figures who fall into that category from the literary and art worlds. Luminaries such as Rudyard Kipling, George Bernard Shaw, H. G. Wells, and James McNeill Whistler come under the author\'s scrutiny, where they meet with equal measures of his characteristic wisdom and good humor.In addition to incisive assessments of well-known individuals (&quot;Mr. Rudyard Kipling and Making the World Small&quot; and &quot;Mr. H. G. Wells and the Giants&quot;), these essays contain observations on the wider world. &quot;On Sandals and Simplicity,&quot; &quot;Science and the Savages,&quot; &quot;On Certain Modern Writers and the Institution of the Family,&quot; &quot;On Smart Novelists and the Smart Set,&quot; and &quot;Slum Novelists and the Slums&quot; reflect the main themes of Chesterton\'s life\'s work. Heretics roused the ire of some critics for censuring contemporary philosophies without providing alternatives; the author responded a few years later with a companion volume, Orthodoxy. Sardonic, jolly, and generous, both books are vintage Chesterton.\n\nHe is criticizing those who hold incomplete and inadequate views about &quot;life, the universe, and everything.&quot; He is, in short, criticizing all that host of non-Christian views of reality, as he demonstrated in his follow-up book Orthodoxy. The book is both an easy read and a difficult read. But he manages to demonstrate, among other things, that our new 21st century heresies are really not new because he himself deals with most of them.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"2611026681147075285\" <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18261663677484787401"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br/><br/><br/>Clive Staples Lewis was one of the intellectual giants of the twentieth century and arguably one of the most influential writers of his day. He was a Fellow and Tutor in English Literature at Oxford University until 1954. He was unanimously elected to the Chair of Medieval and Renaissance Literature at Cambridge</span>
  <span id="freeText18261663677484787401" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br /><br /><br />Clive Staples Lewis was one of the intellectual giants of the twentieth century and arguably one of the most influential writers of his day. He was a Fellow and Tutor in English Literature at Oxford University until 1954. He was unanimously elected to the Chair of Medieval and Renaissance Literature at Cambridge University, a position he held until his retirement. He wrote more than thirty books, allowing him to reach a vast audience, and his works continue to attract thousands of new readers every year. His most distinguished and popular accomplishments include <i>Mere Christianity</i>, <i>Out of the Silent Planet</i>, <i>The Great Divorce</i>, <i>The Screwtape Letters</i>, and the universally acknowledged classics <i>The Chronicles of Narnia</i>. To date, the Narnia books have sold over 100 million copies and been transformed into three major motion pictures.<br /><br />Lewis was married to poet <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/467360.Joy_Davidman" title="Joy Davidman" rel="nofollow noopener">Joy Davidman</a>.<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1988716._W_H__Lewis" title=" W.H. Lewis" rel="nofollow noopener"> W.H. Lewis</a> was his elder brother]</span>
  <a data-text-id="18261663677484787401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/14816053-the-four-loves">Quotes from The Four Loves</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Friendship ... is born at the moment when one man says to another "What! You too? I thought that no one but myself . . .&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/10554-friendship-is-born-at-the-moment-when-one-man">84901 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;To love at all is to be vulnerable. Love anything and your heart will be wrung and possibly broken. If you want to make sure of keeping it intact you must give it to no one, not even an animal. Wrap it carefully round with hobbies and little luxuries; avoid all entanglements. Lock it up safe in the casket or coffin of your selfishness. But in that casket, safe, dark, motionless, airless, it will change. It will not be broken; it will become unbreakable, impenetrable, irredeemable. To love is to be vulnerable.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/3058-to-love-at-all-is-to-be-vulnerable-love-anything">19327 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
